<p class="MsoNoSpacing" align="center" style="text-align: center;"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: 'book antiqua', palatino;"><b>The Significance of Dipavali<o:p></o:p></b></span></p>
<p class="MsoNoSpacing" align="center" style="text-align: center;"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: 'book antiqua', palatino;"><b>Divine Life Society Publication: </b><span style="color: #0000ff;"><a href="http://www.dlshq.org/discourse/nov2007.htm"><span style="color: #0000ff;"><b>Daily Svadhyaya</b></span></a></span><b> by Sri Swami Chidananda<o:p></o:p></b></span></p>
<p class="MsoNoSpacing" style="text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: 'book antiqua', palatino;">Long ago, our ancients sounded a call asking us to shake ourselves free from the state of sleep where everything is shrouded in darkness. The state of<span class="apple-converted-space"><span style="color: black;">&nbsp;</span></span><i>ajnana</i><span class="apple-converted-space"><i><span style="color: black;">&nbsp;</span></i></span>or the darkness of spiritual ignorance is when one loses Self-awareness. So they gave a call: ‘Awake! Do not be in this state of sleep. Arise, awake, and attain Illumination. Go to those who have become fully awakened. Approach them and ask them to likewise awaken the light within you. Attain full awakenness by humbly approaching worthy teachers.<span class="apple-converted-space"><span style="color: black;">&nbsp;</span></span><i>"Uttishthata jagrata prapya varannibodhata"</i><span class="apple-converted-space"><span style="color: black;">&nbsp;</span></span>[Katha Up. 1.3.14].<i>"Tadviddhi pranipaatena pariprashnena sevayaa"</i><span class="apple-converted-space"><span style="color: black;">&nbsp;</span></span>[Gita 4.34] This great call is the heart of spiritual India. And the significance of Dipavali is a re-enacting of this banishing darkness from within yourself, of shaking yourself free from the sleep of ignorance, and waking up into the light of a new dawn of full awareness. And this is the process you have to work out yourself.</span></p>
<p class="MsoNoSpacing" style="text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: 'book antiqua', palatino;">And to remind you of this, each year the festival of lights is held during the darkest night. It comes as an annual reminder of what you have to do—banish darkness, bring in light, be full of light and revel in the Illumination. Fill yourself with the Light. Fill the whole world with light by your own being in it.</span></p>
<p class="MsoNoSpacing" style="text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: 'book antiqua', palatino;">And to remind us perpetually, they put this great call into our everyday prayer: "<i>Asato Maa Sat-Gamaya, Tamaso Maa Jyotir-Gamaya, Mrityor Maa Amritam-Gamaya</i>"—Lead us from the unreal to the Real; lead us from darkness to Light; lead us from mortality to Immortality." [Brih. Up. 1.3.28] To be in darkness is death. To arise form darkness into Light is to rise up from mortality and death into everlasting life. To awaken the Light within is to break this net of illusion of vanishing names and forms, and rising into full awareness of That which is beyond, That which is Reality. The concluding line of another great<span class="apple-converted-space"><span style="color: black;">&nbsp;</span></span><i>mantra</i><span class="apple-converted-space"><i><span style="color: black;">&nbsp;</span></i></span>supplicates the supreme Divine to manifest His grace within us as Illumination—<i>"Dhiyo Yo Nah Prachodayat</i>—May He illumine our intellects<i>"</i>. We are inheritors of heritage that tells us: You are the Light. Awaken that Light within you. Realise that great Light of lights beyond darkness, and become blessed. Live your life for this ultimate attainment and Experience. Let us claim our birthright and move towards the great Light. This is the supreme rejoicing. May we all thus rejoice!</span></p>
<p class="MsoNoSpacing" align="center" style="text-align: center;">&nbsp;</p>
<p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: .0001pt; line-height: normal;"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: 'book antiqua', palatino;"><span class="MsoHyperlink"><b>&nbsp;Excerpts from: </b></span><b>The Significance of Dipavali<a name="_GoBack"></a> - </b><span style="color: #0000ff;"><a href="http://www.dlshq.org/discourse/nov2007.htm"><span style="color: #0000ff;"><b>Daily Svadhyaya</b></span></a></span></span><b><span style="font-size: 9.0pt;"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: 'book antiqua', palatino;"> by Sri Swami Chidananda</span><o:p></o:p></span></b></p>
<p><span style="font-size: 9pt; font-family: 'book antiqua', palatino;"><span style="color: #000000;" color="#000000" face="Calibri"><span style="color: #333333; font-size: 12pt;">If you would like to purchase the print edition, visit: <strong><span style="color: #0000ff;"><a href="http://www.dlshq.org/download/download.htm"><span style="color: #0000ff;" color="#0066cc">The Divine Life Society E-Bookstore</span></a></span></strong></span></span></span></p>
